She tapped the side of her tablet. The screen behind her showed a glowing schematic—his shoulder, his collarbone, a filigree of **bright alloy**, twisted like a **script**.

His name. And—beneath it—**Alois’s**, carved in delicate loops into the chrome.

> “You’ll carry her now. Even if you forget.”

Jason should’ve shouted. Should’ve pulled against the restraints. Should’ve rejected the entire idea.

Instead—he stared at the screen. And for a second?

He smiled.

* * *

###### Scene 9B: *“Something is Growing in Me”*

There was no light.

Not at first.

Only **warmth**. Gentle. Even. Like floating just below the surface of a still pond.

**Alois’s breath came slow.** Not labored—*measured*. Her chest rose and fell in a rhythm she didn’t set.

She couldn’t feel her arms. Not in a numb way. In a *disconnected* way. Like they were **already doing something without her**.

There was a hum in her skin.

Not sound. **Signal**. Low-frequency. Biological. Like roots murmuring to each other under the soil.

She didn’t try to move. She didn’t try to panic.

The part of her that would normally worry—that would *run diagnostic*, check exits, calculate response—that part was... still. Not gone. Just… **waiting**.

A voice. Soft. Filtered. Calm.

Not in the room. In the floor. In the **walls**.

> “Your system accepted the thread beautifully.”

> “No resistance. You were always meant for resonance.”

Alois’s fingers twitched. Not because she told them to. Because something **called**.

A flush of sensation ran through her arms—not pain, not pleasure. Just **awakening**. The feeling of *being noticed* by your own nervous system.

And underneath her, **the floor breathed back**.

The room was alive.

She could feel **vines behind the walls**. Their vascular data. Their **moisture shifts**. Something flowering somewhere in the next room.

She inhaled. The air was thick with **root scent**, **sterile pollen**, and something sweeter—*Jason’s trace*. Not cologne. Just… proximity.

She didn’t open her eyes. Not yet.

But she smiled.

> *I’m changing.*

> *And I know he’s near.*

* * *

###### Scene: *“You’re Very Good at This”*

He had three fingers disconnected. His left optic had been removed entirely. His chest was open in a **neat Y-shaped spread**, revealing a cascade of wire clusters, one of which was gently pulsing with a melody she hadn’t identified yet.

**Patch grinned.**

He was propped at a slight incline—*deliberately angled*, she’d said, so he could “remain engaged.”

It was charming, really.

Gutlace hovered nearby, four of her limbs active, the others poised like polite questions.

**Gutlace (absently, as she traced a long filigree along his sternum):**

> “Your systems are recursive. But not stable. There’s a feedback pattern here I can’t trace.”

**Patch (beaming):**

> “That’s because I don’t like being legible. It’s a boundary thing.”

She didn’t respond.

She was recording. Constantly.

Patch watched her assistants move—two of them, near silent, masked, dragging carts of delicately sterilized instruments and organ jars labeled in script Patch couldn’t read. They had *grace*, but no improvisation.

**Patch (cheerfully):**

> “Did you know one of your attendants cries in the corridor between scans? Not loudly. Just enough to feel human.”

**Gutlace:**

> “He’s recalibrating. Like you.”

**Patch:**

> “Oh, I’m not recalibrating. I’m *plotting.*”

She paused.

One of her limbs brushed gently along a coil in his neck. She wasn’t cruel. But she wasn’t *not* enjoying this.

**Gutlace:**

> “You’re made of contradiction. It’s inefficient.”

**Patch:**

> “And yet here we are. You, delighted. Me, artistically filleted. Two thinkers working through mutual fascination.”

He rotated one functional eye toward her. His smile sharpened slightly.

> “I don’t want to kill you.”

A pause.

> “But I will outgrow you.”

Gutlace didn’t answer. She didn’t need to. She was already reaching for another tool.

And Patch?

Patch was keeping score.

* * *

###### Scene: *“Carved Into You”*

Jason breathed in slow.

Not groggy. Not disoriented. Just... *level*. The chemical stillness humming beneath his skin muted every reaction. He wasn’t afraid. He wasn’t angry.

He was just *aware*.

Gutlace stood beside him, arms folded, a stylus between two long, gloved fingers. She tapped it gently against her tablet. Not impatient. Just *thoughtful*.

Jason turned his head.

**Left shoulder. Collarbone.**

At first he didn’t see it—just a faint seam, a shift in texture. Then the light hit it right.

**Matte black.**

Angular. *Wedge-shaped*, like a fused brace. Synthetic without being glossy—tactile in a way that felt *intentional*. And there, near the centerline of his clavicle, standing out like paint on glass:

**Alois**

Etched in **gloss pink**.

Not scribbled. Not stamped. **Engraved.**

The letterforms were delicate. Almost feminine. Stylized in a way that looked *coded*. Like a name wrapped in a signature. Like someone meant for it to last.

Jason stared at it. Didn’t blink.

**Gutlace (softly):**

> “Do you like it?”

He didn’t answer at first.

The name caught the light again. *Her* name. Not *his*. But it was on him now.

Always.

**Jason (low):**

> “It’s clean work.”

Gutlace nodded once. No smile. Just satisfaction.

> “I needed to adjust your alignment. And if you're going to carry someone... it should be visible.”

Jason didn’t disagree. He wasn’t sure *why*.

But he didn’t look away.

**Jason:**

> “You could’ve just fixed the tension.”

**Gutlace:**

> “Fixing isn’t enough. I make things better.”

She tilted her head.

> “You’re stronger now. You’ll find that pain means less than it used to. And sentiment—”

She tapped the screen once.

> “Well. It anchors beautifully.”

Jason touched the edge of the metal. The surface was cold.

But the name was warm.

And it felt— Not right.

But *very hard to argue with*.

* * *

###### Scene 12: *“Rooted”*

Alois woke in the **heart of the Garden**.

She wasn’t strapped down. There were no monitors. No restraints. Just the soft pressure of moss-textured weave beneath her palms, and the **gentle weight of vines** laid across her shoulders like ceremonial sashes.

She sat up slowly.

**The air shimmered with moisture**—warm, rich, alive. Light bled softly through the overhead canopy, not from bulbs, but from **veined petals**, glowing faintly in pinks and pale golds.

And the Garden... *breathed*.

She could feel it. Not metaphorically.

**Actually.**

There were root systems in the walls—she could feel the **water coursing through them**. She didn’t hear it. She *felt the temperature shift* through her skin. She could sense **where the humidity was pooling**, which plants were under stress, and which ones were growing toward her.

Alois raised her hand.

Veins in her forearm pulsed **slightly too bright** under her skin—**not green, not red, but a faint opalescent thread**, woven in a pattern she hadn’t asked for.

She pressed her fingers to the floor. The moss responded. Not recoiling. Not obeying. Just... *tuning to her presence*.

**Alois (quiet):**

> “What did you do to me…”

From the walls, a voice answered.

**Gutlace (gently):**

> “I gave you access.”

Alois turned.

The walls did not open. They *peeled*. Vines retracted like curtains, revealing Gutlace’s silhouette behind a living veil of slow-blooming leaves.

She didn’t approach.

She just spoke.

> “The Garden used to ignore you. Now it listens.”

Alois didn’t move.

Her hands flexed. The roots beneath her shifted in response.

**Alois:**

> “Why?”

**Gutlace:**

> “Because you’re worth cultivating. Oh, and you have a mycelial gland. Drink water regularly. ”

The vines near her wrists trembled—just slightly. *As if they agreed.*

* * *

###### Scene: *“Nest”*

Springlee didn’t move. He couldn’t risk it.

The panel above him had stopped dripping maybe six minutes ago, but he didn’t trust it yet. One of Ruckspin’s brutes had walked past not long after the last droplet hit his head, dragging some kind of modular cannon behind him like a toy.

Springlee didn’t want to know what floor it used to be attached to.

He exhaled—*slow*—and shifted a little deeper into the curve of the pipe.

It wasn’t a vent, not really. It was a **structural coolant corridor**, one of the old backbone tubes that still had copper teeth on the inner welds. His fur was getting shredded. He didn’t care.

He adjusted the strap across his chest, checking the pods.

**Five still secure.** The cracked one—**Brush-Faced Weaver**—had stopped twitching. Good sign.

**The Honey-Skinned Orphan** was warm. Too warm.

He tapped the pod gently.

**Springlee (soft):**

> “Not yet. I know. I know. But not yet.”

The Orphan didn’t move, but its fur clung to the inner wall like it had been listening.

The corridor creaked. Something deeper in the ship was moving again—maybe a rerouted gravity loop. Or maybe another floor **changing allegiance**.

Springlee winced and leaned his head back against the wall.

**Springlee:**

> “They better be alive.”

He hadn’t heard from anyone in… hours? A day? The systems had gone dark. Holbrook’s signals had flatlined. No chatter. No pulse.

It was just him and the kids.

And the bootsteps he kept outthinking by inches.

He scratched his ear. Looked at the cracked ceiling tile above.

> “I swear, if I get out of this, I’m demanding a garden level suite and at least one waffle-based apology.”

Then—

A flicker.

In his left eye.

**Pill’s voice.**

> **“Springlee.”**

He froze.

**Springlee:**

> “...You bastard.”

> “You’re back?”

> **“Link restored. Jason, Alois, and Patch are stable. You are primary vector for external deployment.”**

He glanced down at the pods.

They pulsed.

**Springlee (exhaling):**

> “Took you long enough.”

> **“Are you ready?”**

Springlee smiled. It wasn’t a nice smile.

**Springlee:**

> “Let’s go ruin somebody’s symmetry.”

* * *

###### Scene: *“Deploy the Creatures”*

Jason lay back against the synthfoam, eyes half-lidded, collarbone humming quietly under the skin.

> “Pill,” he said, “Get me Springlee.”

A beat.

The link clicked.

**Crackling static** filtered through the channel first—then a familiar voice, sharp and dry as always.

**Springlee:**

> “Took you long enough.”

There was a clatter in the background—metallic, wet.

> “I’ve been nesting in a floor drain for an hour. Half the floor smells like vinegar and trauma. One of the pods cracked.”

Jason closed his eyes and exhaled through a grin.

**Jason:**

> “Which one?”

**Springlee:**

> “Brush-Faced Weaver. He’s fine. Pissed off and twitching, but fine.”

**Alois (on the link):**

> “Do you have them all?”

**Springlee:**

> “I’m down to four intact and one leaking. But they’re with me. What’s the move?”

**Pill’s voice came next—clear now, steady.**

> “We are going to inoculate the ship.”

> “Each of them is a presence-seed. They will carry me to the pirate lords, one by one. I will take hold slowly, quietly. They won’t resist. They’ll… align.”

**Patch (gleeful):**

> “We’re not winning the war. We’re rewriting the script.”

Springlee huffed.

> “So which little freak goes where?”

**Jason:**

> “We’ll tell you. But we need to be clean. Quiet. Precise.”

**Pill:**

> “Once three anchors are in place, control will begin to erode. Once five are planted… they’ll agree with us.”

Alois whispered something—more a shape than a word. Jason felt it. So did Patch.

**Jason:**

> “Let’s begin.”

* * *

###### Scene: *“One of Us Now”*

The Garden was still.

Not silent. The vines still moved, and the water systems pulsed behind the walls. But the space had settled into a kind of **consensual stillness**—a ritual calm that didn’t need to be asked for.

Gutlace stood at the far curve of the atrium. Her limbs were retracted. Her gauze mask loose at the edges, but still on.

Jason stood to her right, just out of reach. Alois stood closer.

**Jason (quiet):**

> “It’s done. The floor’s yours, if you want it. But the ship listens to us now.”

Gutlace didn’t flinch. She tilted her head slightly, like she was inspecting a small growth she hadn’t planted.

**Gutlace:**

> “You took me without cutting. That’s elegant.”

Alois stepped forward.

She didn’t speak.

She just **reached up**, slowly, and placed one hand against the edge of Gutlace’s mask.

Gutlace didn’t resist. She let the hand stay.

Her breathing changed—just a little. Not nervous. Not expectant. Just... *aware*.

Alois leaned forward. The air between them was warm. Sweet with root pollen and sterilized humidity.

And then—

**She kissed her.**

Not hard. Not passionate. Just soft. Right below the cheekbone.

A gesture.

A message.

A seal.

Gutlace closed her eyes.

There was no glow. No sound. But Pill moved. Across breath. Across nerve. Across skin.

A moment passed. Then two.

Gutlace opened her eyes. And smiled—small. Tight. *Honest*.

**Gutlace (soft):**

> “I suppose I belong to you now.”

**Alois:**

> “You always did.”

* * *

###### Scene: *“Acknowledged”*

A moment after the kiss—

The lights shifted.

Not brighter. Not dimmer.

Just **realigned**.

The overhead blossoms dimmed in certain zones. Vines retracted from Gutlace’s shoulders and **coiled slightly toward Alois**. The airflow adjusted. The scent profile shifted.

Jason felt it first in his chest—a low pulse of atmospheric feedback he hadn’t noticed before.

**Pill (calm, present):**

> “She is integrated.”

> “Emotional authority of the floor has been reassigned.”

**Gutlace turned her head slowly, watching the way the vines followed Alois’s hand.**

She didn’t protest.

She just **smiled faintly**, and adjusted the wrist of her glove.

**Gutlace:**

> “I’ll need to recalibrate my protocols.”

**Jason:**

> “You’re not in charge anymore.”

**Gutlace:**

> “No. But I’m still useful.”

**Alois (quietly):**

> “Then come with us.”

The Garden didn’t breathe them out.

It **opened the path**.

* * *

**SIGNALS FROM THE EDGE** *The Consecration of Unwinding*

---

The cargo bay had been repurposed as a surgical theater. Not because Gutlace requested it—she had made no requests since the agreement—but because Jason understood what was required. Space. Witness. The gravity of undoing.

Seventeen bodies lay in suspension cradles, their breathing synchronized to a rhythm that was not their own. Gutlace moved between them with a precision that looked like tenderness but wasn't. Not yet. Her mycelial fingers—translucent, branching—hovered over the first sleeper: a Krovist male whose carapace had gone soft where the spores had nested deepest.

Alois stood at the threshold, arms crossed. Not watching Gutlace. Watching Jason, who watched Gutlace like he was afraid she might change her mind.

"You know what this costs me," Gutlace said. Not to either of them. To the air between all three.

"Yes," Jason said.

"Then you know I have never been alone."

Alois spoke for the first time since they'd entered. "You will be now."

Gutlace's cap—the broad fungal crown that served as both skull and broadcast organ—dimmed. A shudder passed through her body, visible as tremor in the threads that connected her to the seventeen. For six decades she had known their hungers before they felt them. Their fears as they formed. She had been a chorus wearing surgical gloves.

"Begin," Jason said. Gentle. Unyielding.

Gutlace's fingers sank into the Krovist's skull at the soft-point juncture. Not cutting. *Unweaving.* The spore network pulsed once, sending a flare of bioluminescence through the cargo bay—gold, then green, then the blue of something dying cleanly.

The Krovist's breathing broke rhythm.

His eyes opened.

For three seconds, there was only confusion. Then recognition arrived, and with it, horror. He tried to scream but his throat had forgotten how. The sound that came out was a kit-bird's shriek, high and shattered.

"Hold him," Gutlace said.

Jason moved before Alois could. His hands on the Krovist's shoulders, firm but not forceful. "You're safe. You're awake. You're *you* again."

The Krovist stared at Jason's face like he'd never seen another being before. Perhaps he hadn't. Not with his own eyes.

"What did you—what did she—" The words wouldn't form right. Sixty years of not needing syntax.

"She gave you back," Alois said from the threshold. Still not moving closer. "Whether you wanted it or not."

Gutlace had already moved to the second cradle. A Tlassi engineer whose tendrils had been repurposed as neural relays. She didn't speak again. Didn't pause. Her fingers found the node-points, the places where her children—she had always called them her children—had rooted deepest.

The second unweaving was faster. The Tlassi woke thrashing, keening in a frequency that made the cradle's metal sing. Jason stayed with the Krovist, murmuring low, while Alois finally stepped forward to hold the Tlassi's tendrils before they could damage themselves against the restraints.

"Breathe," Alois said. Command, not comfort. "You're going to want to tear yourself apart. Don't."

By the fifth awakening, Gutlace was trembling. By the ninth, she had to stop. Her cap had gone nearly black, the bioluminescence faded to ember-glow. She stood between two cradles, mycelial fingers dripping the clear fluid that passed for her blood.

"I can feel them leaving," she said. "Every thread I sever, I am—" She stopped. Started again. "I am becoming singular."

Jason left the Krovist, who had curled into himself, rocking. He stood beside Gutlace but didn't touch her. Knew better.

"Is it agony?" he asked.

"No." Gutlace's voice was different now. Thinner. More alone. "It is *reduction*. I was a forest. Now I am a single tree, watching my canopy burn."

"You were a slaver," Alois said from across the bay. Not cruel. Factual. "Now you're a surgeon who used to be a slaver."

Gutlace turned to look at her. The gesture was slower than it should have been, like she was learning her body's weight for the first time.

"Yes," Gutlace said. "I was."

She returned to the work.

---

By the fourteenth awakening, the cargo bay had become a chorus of grief. Some of the freed wept. Others raged. One—a Vellan whose species did not have words for what they felt—simply stood in the center of the bay and keened, a sound like wind through a world that had ended.

Gutlace worked through it all. Jason and Alois moved between the awakened, holding, guiding, containing the violence of returned autonomy. No one thanked Gutlace. Several tried to kill her. Jason stopped them, but barely, and only with words: *"She's ending herself to free you. Let her finish."*

The seventeenth was a human. Young. Maybe twenty standard years, though it was hard to tell—the spores had kept her body in stasis, ageless and obedient.

When Gutlace withdrew the final thread, the girl didn't scream. Didn't thrash. She opened her eyes and looked directly at Gutlace with an expression that was not gratitude or rage but something worse: *recognition*.

"You were kind," the girl whispered. "When you took me. You made it not hurt."

Gutlace's fingers stilled. For the first time since the work began, she looked like she might speak. Might defend herself. Might explain that kindness in the taking did not excuse the taking itself.

She said nothing.

The girl closed her eyes again. Began to cry.

---

When it was finished, Gutlace stood in the center of the cargo bay, surrounded by seventeen beings who were no longer hers. Her cap had gone fully dark. The mycelial network that had once branched through her arms and spine had withdrawn, leaving her body clean-edged, defined, *alone*.

Jason approached slowly. Alois stayed back, watching.

"It's done," Gutlace said. Not a question.

"It's done," Jason confirmed.

"I can't hear them anymore."

"No."

"I don't know who I am without them."

Jason was quiet for a long moment. Then: "Neither do they. You'll figure it out together. Separately."

Gutlace looked at him. Her eyes—compound, faceted—reflected his face seventeen times over.

"You knew this would unmake me."

"Yes."

"And you required it anyway."

"Yes."

She nodded once. Turned to look at the awakened, who would not look back at her. Who were learning the shape of their own thoughts, the boundaries of their own skin.

"Then I am yours," Gutlace said quietly. "By choice now. Not by colony. Not by network. By the thing I became when I let them go."

Alois finally stepped forward. Stood beside Jason, a united front.

"We don't want you by ownership," Alois said. "We want you by truth. Can you give us that?"

Gutlace's cap flickered once—dim gold, like a candle in a vast room.

"I can try," she said.

It was the first honest thing she'd said since boarding.

---

**END SCENE**
